<p><i><b>Me. I Am Mariah... The Elusive Chanteuse</b></i> is the fourteenth studio album by American singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>. It was released on May 23, 2014, through <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a>, her final album on the label. The record had been in development since 2011; during its production, Carey hired friend and collaborator <a href="/wiki/Randy_Jackson" title="Randy Jackson">Randy Jackson</a> to manage her career, before replacing him with another frequent collaborator, <a href="/wiki/Jermaine_Dupri" title="Jermaine Dupri">Jermaine Dupri</a>. The album consists of guest appearances from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nas_(rapper)" title="Nas (rapper)">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_(singer)" title="Miguel (singer)">Miguel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wale_(rapper)" title="Wale (rapper)">Wale</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fabolous" title="Fabolous">Fabolous</a>, in addition to Carey's twins Morroccan and Monroe. On the deluxe edition of the album, <a href="/wiki/R._Kelly" title="R. Kelly">R. Kelly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a> respectively make appearances on remixes of two songs taken from Carey's twelfth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Memoirs_of_an_Imperfect_Angel" title="Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel">Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel</a></i> (2009).</p>
<p>Previously titled <i>The Art of Letting Go</i>, the album was originally scheduled for release in 2012 following the single, "<a href="/wiki/Triumphant_(Get_%27Em)" title="Triumphant (Get 'Em)">Triumphant (Get 'Em)</a>" featuring <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a>. However, after the song's underperformance, additional songs were recorded for the album, causing the release date to be pushed back several times throughout 2013 and again in 2014. Together with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bryan_Michael_Cox" title="Bryan Michael Cox">Bryan Michael Cox</a>, Carey and Dupri <a href="/wiki/Executive_producer" title="Executive producer">executively produced</a> the album. It is named after a self-portrait that Carey drew at the age of three-years old that she captioned "Me. I Am Mariah". "The Elusive Chanteuse" part of the title is one of Carey's many <a href="/wiki/Nickname" title="Nickname">monikers</a>.</p>
<p>After its release, the album was critically appreciated but was a commercial disappointment, becoming the lowest selling release of Carey's career. <i>Me. I Am Mariah...</i> was promoted through a number of media appearances by Carey as well as <a href="/wiki/The_Elusive_Chanteuse_Show" title="The Elusive Chanteuse Show">The Elusive Chanteuse Show</a>. Four singles were released from the album including, the <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">Australian</a> top-ten and US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> top-twenty hit "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Beautiful (Mariah Carey song)">#Beautiful</a>" (a duet with <a href="/wiki/Miguel_(singer)" title="Miguel (singer)">Miguel</a>), as well as the less successful "<a href="/wiki/The_Art_of_Letting_Go" title="The Art of Letting Go">The Art of Letting Go</a>", "<a href="/wiki/You%27re_Mine_(Eternal)" title="You're Mine (Eternal)">You're Mine (Eternal)</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/You_Don%27t_Know_What_to_Do" title="You Don't Know What to Do">You Don't Know What to Do</a>" featuring rapper Wale.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On September 25, 2009, Carey's twelfth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Memoirs_of_an_Imperfect_Angel" title="Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel">Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel</a></i>, was released. Following the cancellation of <i>Angels Advocate</i>, a remix album of <i>Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel</i>, it was announced that Carey would return to the studio to start work on her thirteenth studio album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-return_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-return-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> It was later revealed that it would be her second Christmas album, the follow-up to <i><a href="/wiki/Merry_Christmas_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Merry Christmas (Mariah Carey album)">Merry Christmas</a></i> (1994). The album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Merry_Christmas_II_You" title="Merry Christmas II You">Merry Christmas II You</a></i>, was released alongside an accompanying DVD, and was sent to <a href="/wiki/Retail" title="Retail">retailers</a> on November 2, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Merry Christmas II You</i> debuted at number four on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with sales of 56,000 copies, surpassing the opening week sales of Carey's previous holiday album of 45,000 copies 16 years prior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opening_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-opening-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> It also became Carey's 16th top ten album in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opening_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-opening-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> The album debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Top_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums">R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a> chart, making it only the second Christmas album to top this chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the birth of her children, Carey began work on her fourteenth studio album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first indication that Carey had begun work on her fourteenth studio album was in February 2011, with Carey stating: "I start writing for my new album this week-but it's just the beginning...."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 2011, Carey's representative said she will donate royalties for the song "Save the Day", which she has written for her upcoming studio album, to charities that create awareness for human-rights issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Her husband <a href="/wiki/Nick_Cannon" title="Nick Cannon">Nick Cannon</a> told <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> in May 2011 that Carey had already completed a good amount of recording for a new album, a few months before during her pregnancy: "She's planning on having a [new single] out this year. She's been working away, and we have a studio in the crib, and [the pregnancy] has totally inspired her on so many different levels." Additionally, Cannon confirmed that Carey was inspired by her debut <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey_(album)" title="Mariah Carey (album)">self-titled album</a> and its follow-up, <i><a href="/wiki/Emotions_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Emotions (Mariah Carey album)">Emotions</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2012, Cannon updated everyone on the album, saying: "My beautiful wife is planning to make her return to the music scene after taking time off to focus on the pregnancy and the birth of our two wonderful babies, Moroccan and Monroe."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> On August 3, 2012, Carey released "<a href="/wiki/Triumphant_(Get_%27Em)" title="Triumphant (Get 'Em)">Triumphant (Get 'Em)</a>", a collaboration with rappers <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a>, which was originally claimed to be the <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a> for her upcoming studio album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The single received low impact both critically and commercially, and was eventually removed the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Island_Def_Jam_Music_Group" title="The Island Def Jam Music Group">The Island Def Jam Music Group</a> was shuttered by <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a> on April 1, 2014. <a href="/wiki/Island_Records" title="Island Records">Island Records</a> and <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a> operate as separate entities, with Carey being transferred from Island to Def Jam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording">Recording</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Recording">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In September 2011, producer and friend <a href="/wiki/Jermaine_Dupri" title="Jermaine Dupri">Jermaine Dupri</a> took to his social network Global14 to reveal that he's back in the studio with Carey working on new music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> In July 2012, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Randy_Jackson" title="Randy Jackson">Randy Jackson</a> completed seven songs with Carey for the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 2012, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bryan_Michael_Cox" title="Bryan Michael Cox">Bryan Michael Cox</a> said about the album: "She was committed to making it before she got pregnant. Then she got pregnant and she took the time off. Then after she came back, we started really vibing again and we picked up right where we left off. I just feel like between [record producer] Jermaine Dupri, myself and her, we came up with a few things that [are] really, really a solid body of work".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2012, Carey was in the studio with <a href="/wiki/R._Kelly" title="R. Kelly">R. Kelly</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carey said about her fourteenth studio album: "I'm collaborating with a lot of my favorite people but the main thing is [that] I'm not trying to follow any particular trend, I want it to be well received. I want to stay true to myself and the music that I love and make the fans happy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Some of the people that Carey worked with on the album include: <a href="/wiki/DJ_Clue%3F" title="DJ Clue?">DJ Clue?</a>, <a href="/wiki/Randy_Jackson" title="Randy Jackson">Randy Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Q-Tip_(musician)" title="Q-Tip (musician)">Q-Tip</a>, <a href="/wiki/R._Kelly" title="R. Kelly">R. Kelly</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Morales" title="David Morales">David Morales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loris_Holland" title="Loris Holland">Loris Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stevie_J" title="Stevie J">Stevie J</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Fauntleroy" title="James Fauntleroy">James Fauntleroy</a>, Ray Angry, <a href="/wiki/Jermaine_Dupri" title="Jermaine Dupri">Jermaine Dupri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryan-Michael_Cox" title="Bryan-Michael Cox">Bryan-Michael Cox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sounds_of_Blackness" title="Sounds of Blackness">James "Big Jim" Wright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hit-Boy" title="Hit-Boy">Hit-Boy</a>, <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Da_Brat" title="Da Brat">Da Brat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Jerkins" title="Rodney Jerkins">Rodney Jerkins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OMG_Yahoo_R._Kelly_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-OMG_Yahoo_R._Kelly-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardexclusive_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboardexclusive-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carey gave <i>Billboard</i> an exclusive interview in their March 9, 2013 issue, stating: "It's about making sure I have tons of good music, because at the end of the day, that's the most important thing.... There are a lot more raw ballads than people might expect... there are also uptempo and signature-type songs that represent [my] different facets as an artist.... Wherever we go with this project, I've tried to keep the soul and heart in it." <i>Billboard</i> also asked Carey about the title of the album, but she declined to reveal it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardexclusive_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboardexclusive-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> In late March 2013, Carey stated that she "has more than enough songs" but "she's in the process of finishing things and mixing and all that".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On June 20, 2013; Carey was in the studio with <a href="/wiki/Mike_Will_Made_It" title="Mike Will Made It">Mike Will Made It</a> and <a href="/wiki/Young_Jeezy" title="Young Jeezy">Young Jeezy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> On August 3, 2013, Carey was in the studio with rapper <a href="/wiki/Wale_(rapper)" title="Wale (rapper)">Wale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2013, Carey was in the studio with rapper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nas_(rapper)" title="Nas (rapper)">Nas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 2013, Jermaine Dupri was announced as Carey's new manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> In January 2014, Carey stated that there will be two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cover_songs" title="Cover songs">cover songs</a> on the album and announced that she has finished sequencing the album's track list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview in February 2014, Carey added that there are songs on the album that are about her husband Nick Cannon<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as songs that she wrote specifically for her twins Moroccan and Monroe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> That same month, Carey announced to <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a> that she has added three new songs to the tracklist, 1 extra Hitboy record and two new remixes<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> and stated that she is in the process of choosing a new title for the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The two remixes are of the songs "Betcha Gon' Know" and "It's a Wrap", previously featured on 2009's <i><a href="/wiki/Memoirs_of_an_Imperfect_Angel" title="Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel">Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel</a></i>; <a href="/wiki/R._Kelly" title="R. Kelly">R. Kelly</a> features on the former, while <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a> features on the latter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Details_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Details-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The cover versions were confirmed to be <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>'s 1988 single, "<a href="/wiki/One_More_Try_(George_Michael_song)" title="One More Try (George Michael song)">One More Try</a>", and cover of the patriotic song "<a href="/wiki/America_the_Beautiful" title="America the Beautiful">America the Beautiful</a>" for the Japanese CD edition of the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Details_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Details-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jap_CD_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jap_CD-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_lyrics">Music and lyrics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Music and lyrics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:24%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 89%; background-color: #FFFFF0;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div style="margin:0px 2em;">
<p>The music reacts to Carey's fallow years in most every way it should. It returns her to the type of grand balladry, and formal melodies, that first made her a star. It's her most melodic, least-trendy album in memory — both moves that greatly flatter her.</p>
</div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">“</div>
<div style="position: absolute; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">”</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: right;"> — Jim Farber, <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" title="Daily News (New York)">New York Daily News</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nydailynews_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-nydailynews-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>Consisting of fifteen songs and four deluxe songs <i>Me. I Am Mariah... The Elusive Chanteuse</i> is an R&amp;B album with a diverse musical style that incorporates <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newsday_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newsday-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_soul" title="Hip hop soul">hip hop soul</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yahoo_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Entertainment_Weekly_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Entertainment_Weekly-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> and elements of <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gawker_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gawker-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vibe_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vibe-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Mike Wass of Idolator described the album as being a concept album that journeys through the era's of R&amp;B, from Motown to the '90s, disco and early hip-hop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Described by Sarah Rodman as being a "rhythmic hip-hop pop" album that contains "gospel-inflected power ballads, old-school soul, and straight-up disco fantasias," Rodman described the album's production as being built over a "pulsating atmosphere" and "fidgety rhythmic tracks."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Jim Farber of <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" title="Daily News (New York)">New York Daily News</a></i> cited the album as a return from her previous studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Memoirs_of_an_Imperfect_Angel" title="Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel">Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel</a></i> (2009), which Fader described as a "disastrous", Farber noted the album's musical content as containing "grand balladry, and formal melodies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nydailynews_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-nydailynews-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Melissa Maerz of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i>, noted "nostalgia" to be a big and recurring theme both lyrically and musically, continuing to comment on this saying the "arrangements that borrow from Inner Life's disco rave-up 'I'm Caught Up (In a One Night Love Affair)' and the O'Jays' Philly-soul classic 'Let Me Make Love to You'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-entertainmentweekly_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-entertainmentweekly-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Eric Henderson of <i>Slant Magazine</i> noted the album's lyrics to be "personal, crazy. Crazy personal," Henderson continued calling the album's lyrical content an "deliberately confusing innocence with insight, obliviousness with bliss."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slantmagazine1_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-slantmagazine1-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey's voice on the album was described by Elysa Gardner of <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>, as "artful melisma, robust belting and decorative high notes." Gardner continued, noting Mariah's use of her "supple middle and lower registers to convey feeling simply and directly."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The album opens with "Cry", a gospel song built over a piano, "simmering vocals and full-bodied runs" containing "swirling organs and scaling ad-lib."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Described by Billboard magazine as being one of the album's most "heaviest moments," lyrically the song discusses Carey's desire to hold a lover until they both start "bawling."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> "Faded" is a "luscious" R&amp;B song produced by Mike Will Made It, the song and Carey's vocals feature "climaxes" with the song taking influence from R&amp;B hip-hop and pop genres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> "Dedicated" features American rapper <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, the song contains a sample from "Da Mystery of Chessboxin'" as performed by <a href="/wiki/Wu-Tang_Clan" title="Wu-Tang Clan">Wu-Tang Clan</a> and lyrically discusses nostalgia, with Mariah and Nas looking back at their past relationships and how they have shaped their lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> "#Beautiful" is a mid-tempo and stripped down <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> music song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LA_Times_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Lipshutz_Review_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Lipshutz_Review-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Idolator_Review_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Idolator_Review-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey's "big vocals" combined with Miguel's "signature eclectic rock and roll sound" results in "#Beautiful" having an old school vibe to it reminiscent of the <a href="/wiki/Stax_Records" title="Stax Records">Stax Records</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motown_Records" title="Motown Records">Motown Records</a> era,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA_Today_Mansfield_Review_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-USA_Today_Mansfield_Review-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> according to a reviewer for The Honesty Hour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Honesty_Hour_Review_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Honesty_Hour_Review-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"Thirsty" is a "club-friendly" <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> song, which lasts for a duration of three minutes and 26 seconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slant_Review_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slant_Review-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thirsty_Idolator_1_Lee_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thirsty_Idolator_1_Lee-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Me_I_Am_Mariah_UK_iTunes_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Me_I_Am_Mariah_UK_iTunes-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> "Thirsty" is about how Carey's lover has a thirst for fame which causes her to drown in her own misery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hitfix_Review_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hitfix_Review-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> American rapper <a href="/wiki/Rich_Homie_Quan" title="Rich Homie Quan">Rich Homie Quan</a> performs background chants on "Thirsty", although he is not credited on the album track list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thirsty_Idolator_1_Lee_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Thirsty_Idolator_1_Lee-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> He does, however, appear as a featured artist on a shortened alternate version of the song, and performs one rap verse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hitfix_Review_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hitfix_Review-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> "Make It Look Good," lyrically talks about "getting played" by a man yet she is deciding "to just go with it," the song is built over a "skipping '80's" beat that contains interpolations of "Let Me Make Love to You", written by <a href="/wiki/Bunny_Sigler" title="Bunny Sigler">Walter "Bunny" Sigler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allan_Felder" title="Allan Felder">Allan Felder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> "You're Mine (Eternal)" is a <a href="/wiki/Love_song" title="Love song">love song</a> which lasts for a duration of three minutes and forty-two seconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Christina_Garibaldi_MTV_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Christina_Garibaldi_MTV-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iTunes_Original_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-iTunes_Original-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The song utilizes an hypnotic and "smooth, steady" beat, which slowly but gradually builds to a sudden climax at the end. Lyrically, the track features Carey reminiscing about a past lover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Christina_Garibaldi_MTV_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-Christina_Garibaldi_MTV-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"You Don't Know What to Do" features American rapper Wale and contains interpolations of "I'm Caught Up in a One Night Love Affair", written by <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Adams_(musician)" title="Patrick Adams (musician)">Patrick Adams</a> and Terri Gonzalez.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-2"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> The song is a disco inspired track containing a "bumping" beat compared to music of 1977.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_49-3"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> "Supernatural" is a "sappy cut" featuring Carey's children credited as "Dem Babies".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_49-4"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> "Meteorite" is built over a "disco beat", lyrically the song is a running "commentary on celebrity culture", and contains a sample from "Goin' Up in Smoke", performed by Eddie Kendricks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_49-5"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-3"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> "Camouflage" is a piano ballad,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_49-6"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> followed by "Money" featuring rapper Fabulous and features a sample from "Alabeke", performed by Dan Snatch, and "Rapper Dapper Snapper" performed by Edwin Birdsong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-4"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>"Money" is an R&amp;B song built over a "thumping" beat produced by Hit-Boy with lyrics that revolve around money not being important.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_49-7"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>"One More Try" is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cover_song" title="Cover song">cover</a> of <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>'s 1988 single <a href="/wiki/One_More_Try_(George_Michael_song)" title="One More Try (George Michael song)">of the same name</a>, with an "'80s taste" and a "schmaltzy" production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_49-8"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> "Heavenly (No Ways Tired / Can't Give Up Now)" is a gospel song with a choir that is dedicated as a tribute to the late Reverend <a href="/wiki/James_Cleveland" title="James Cleveland">James Cleveland</a>. It contains an excerpt from the Reverend's sermon "God's Promise" performed by James Cleveland. The song also contains a sample of "Can't Give Up Now" performed by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Mary" title="Mary Mary">Mary Mary</a>, "I Don't Feel No Ways Tired" performed by James Cleveland and "Good Ole Music" performed by <a href="/wiki/Funkadelic" title="Funkadelic">Funkadelic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_49-9"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-5"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The deluxe album consists of four extra songs; the opening track "It's A Wrap" features American singer <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>. The song contains a sample of "I Belong to You" by <a href="/wiki/Barry_White" title="Barry White">Barry White</a>, performed by the Love Unlimited Orchestra.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-6"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Betcha_Gon%27_Know_(The_Prologue)" title="Betcha Gon' Know (The Prologue)">Betcha Gon' Know</a>" was originally recorded and included on Carey's 2009 album <i><a href="/wiki/Memoirs_of_an_Imperfect_Angel" title="Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel">Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel</a></i>, the remix featuring R. Kelly leaked in July 2011, and draws influence from <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bain_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bain-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey announced that the remix would appear the album as a deluxe edition bonus track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-I_Am_Mariah_Billboard_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-I_Am_Mariah_Billboard-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> "The Art of Letting Go" is an empowering <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a> and classic <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> ballad with use of <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">the piano</a>, <a href="/wiki/String_(music)" title="String (music)">strings</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guitar" title="Guitar">guitar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The lyrics of the song talk about a personal experience Carey faced throughout the years, possibly including the early days in her career when she was signed to <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a> through her relationship with her then-husband, the former executive of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Music" title="Sony Music">Sony Music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Mottola" title="Tommy Mottola">Tommy Mottola</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The song was originally the inspiration to also call the album <i>The Art of Letting Go</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> however, during in interview with <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> in February 2014, Carey revealed that she was frustrated that the album title leaked as she had not intended for the public to know about it just yet, and as a result she would be retitling the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Title_and_artwork">Title and artwork</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Title and artwork">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In June 2013, it was announced that Carey is "still choosing between two titles" for the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> On June 16, 2013, <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> put the album up for pre-order and revealed its title as <i>The Art of Letting Go</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The following day, producer <a href="/wiki/Jermaine_Dupri" title="Jermaine Dupri">Jermaine Dupri</a> confirmed that Walmart was correct and that the album would be called <i>The Art of Letting Go</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 2014, Carey expressed dismay that the album's title had leaked and confirmed that a new title would now be chosen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The album is now titled <i>Me. I Am Mariah... The Elusive Chanteuse</i>, a two-part title taking its name from two things personal to Carey. The first part is the caption from Carey's "first and only self-portrait", a drawing she drew as a child which is included as part of the album's back cover, while the second half is a nickname she's adopted recently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Details_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Details-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Summarizing the title and album's concept, Carey said "This album is a reflection of some of the peaks and valleys that made me who I am today. I've always known me. I am Mariah."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_Magazine_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-US_Magazine-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Carl Williot from <a href="/wiki/Idolator_(website)" title="Idolator (website)">Idolator</a> called the album title both "absurd" and "insane". He also lambasted Carey for including "annoying" punctuation in the track listing, including a <a href="/wiki/Hashtag" title="Hashtag">hashtag</a> (#) for the song "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Beautiful (Mariah Carey song)">#Beautiful</a>", a <a href="/wiki/Full_stop" title="Full stop">period</a> (.) for the song "Cry." and appending characters to the song "Money ($ * / ...)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> '​s Dan Macsai called it the "greatest, most over-the-top album title of all time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On the standard edition cover, Carey poses with her arms behind her head, while wearing a nude-colored crocheted swimsuit. The deluxe edition features a close-up of Carey's face, on the same sun-kissed background.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_Magazine_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-US_Magazine-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Jeremy Blacklow from <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Music" title="Yahoo! Music">Yahoo! Music</a> commented that some fans felt that the album covers "look retouched to the extreme".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the April 2012 issue of <i>Shape</i> magazine, Carey stated: "I've started writing songs for a new album, which I hope will come out in 2012. Getting back in the studio and making music again-which I truly love doing-is the best way to end this crazy year".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 2012, Carey's then-manager <a href="/wiki/Randy_Jackson" title="Randy Jackson">Randy Jackson</a> told <i>Billboard</i> that the album was set for release in March 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey told <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Seacrest" title="Ryan Seacrest">Ryan Seacrest</a> in September 2012: "I want[ed] [it] to [be released] sooner, but I guess it wouldn't be ready until around January 2013, somewhere around there. I wanted to put another single out, a ballad. I love it, but I'm still writing, I'm still working. So, you never know what it's going to end up being".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2013, Carey stated that she wanted to release the album as soon as possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was delayed to May 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> which soon changed to July 23, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard1_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard1-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the album was again delayed. On February 10, 2014, it was announced that the album was then set for release on May 6, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey discussed issues around the failed singles and push backs during an interview with <i>Billboard</i>, for the magazine's cover story. She said that she wanted fans to hear the album as a full body of work and thus performance of individual singles was less important.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Cover_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Cover-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey also considered a "<a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>-style surprise digital release" – Beyoncé released her <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_(album)" title="Beyoncé (album)">self-titled album</a> to the <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a> in December 2013 without any prior warning, but Def Jam confirmed that Carey's album would receive a traditional release with pre-orders starting May 1, 2014 and a pre-announced album cover, track listing and release date for May 27, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Cover_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Cover-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The album served as Carey's final release under her deal with Def Jam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">Promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_(Live_@_GMA,_May_24,_2013).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_%28Live_%40_GMA%2C_May_24%2C_2013%29.JPG/220px-Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_%28Live_%40_GMA%2C_May_24%2C_2013%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_%28Live_%40_GMA%2C_May_24%2C_2013%29.JPG/330px-Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_%28Live_%40_GMA%2C_May_24%2C_2013%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_%28Live_%40_GMA%2C_May_24%2C_2013%29.JPG/440px-Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_%28Live_%40_GMA%2C_May_24%2C_2013%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_(Live_@_GMA,_May_24,_2013).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carey singing "#Beautiful" live on <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i>, May 24, 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Elusive_Chanteuse_Show" title="The Elusive Chanteuse Show">The Elusive Chanteuse Show</a></div>
<p>Carey taped a performance of "#Beautiful" along with a medley of her greatest hits on May 15, 2013. The medley included Carey's debut "<a href="/wiki/Vision_of_Love" title="Vision of Love">Vision of Love</a>", as well as other songs such as "<a href="/wiki/Make_It_Happen_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Make It Happen (Mariah Carey song)">Make it Happen</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/We_Belong_Together_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="We Belong Together (Mariah Carey song)">We Belong Together</a>", "<a href="/wiki/My_All" title="My All">My All</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Hero_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Hero (Mariah Carey song)">Hero</a>". The taping aired the following day (May 16) during the <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> Season 12 finale episode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey performed "#Beautiful" with Miguel on June 2, 2013, at Hot 97's Summer Jam XX festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> She performed the remix of the song with <a href="/wiki/Young_Jeezy" title="Young Jeezy">Young Jeezy</a> and Miguel on June 30, 2013, at the <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards" title="BET Awards">BET Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The singer taped a performance of "The Art of Letting Go", along with a medley of "<a href="/wiki/Auld_Lang_Syne" title="Auld Lang Syne">Auld Lang Syne</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Fantasy_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Fantasy (Mariah Carey song)">Fantasy</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Honey_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Honey (Mariah Carey song)">Honey</a>", "#Beautiful", "<a href="/wiki/Emotions_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Emotions (Mariah Carey song)">Emotions</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Always_Be_My_Baby" title="Always Be My Baby">Always Be My Baby</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Touch_My_Body_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Touch My Body (Mariah Carey song)">Touch My Body</a>" and "We Belong Together", for <i><a href="/wiki/Dick_Clark%27s_New_Year%27s_Rockin%27_Eve" title="Dick Clark's New Year's Rockin' Eve">Dick Clark's New Year's Rockin' Eve</a></i>, which aired on December 31, 2013. Carey performed "You're Mine (Eternal)" for the first time at the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television" title="Black Entertainment Television">BET</a></i> Honors on February 8, 2014 and the show premiered on TV Monday February 24, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> On February 13, 2014, Carey performed the song live while lighting up the <a href="/wiki/Empire_State_Building" title="Empire State Building">Empire State Building</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey opened the <a href="/wiki/2014_World_Music_Awards" title="2014 World Music Awards">2014 World Music Awards</a> with a performance of "Meteorite" and received Pop Icon Awards for having sold over 200 million records, and having more number one singles in United States than any other solo artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Beautiful (Mariah Carey song)">#Beautiful</a>" was released as the album's <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a> on May 7, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FMQB_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FMQB-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> "#Beautiful" made its debut on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 chart at number 24, the highest debut of the week. It has since peaked at 15, becoming Carey's 33rd Top 20 Hit, and being one of only 5 to miss the Top 10. It also gave Miguel his 3rd Top 20 hit, after Power Trip (2013) and Adorn (2012).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hot_100_and_Digital_Debuts_and_Tallies_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hot_100_and_Digital_Debuts_and_Tallies-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>, "#Beautiful" had sold 1.2 million copies in the United States as of April 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USsales_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-USsales-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Internationally, the song reached the top-ten position in Australia, Croatia, Denmark, New Zealand, South Africa, and South Korea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> The music video for "#Beautiful" was directed by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kahn" title="Joseph Kahn">Joseph Kahn</a>. It was filmed on April 21 and 22, 2013. The video was supposed to have its world premiere on <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> on May 8, 2013, however, the release date was pushed back to May 9, 2013 instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Lipshutz_Review_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Lipshutz_Review-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> It was made available to view on <a href="/wiki/Vevo" title="Vevo">Vevo</a> and <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> immediately after its television debut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Lipshutz_Review_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Lipshutz_Review-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The album's second single, "<a href="/wiki/The_Art_of_Letting_Go" title="The Art of Letting Go">The Art of Letting Go</a>", had its world premiere via <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> on November 11, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Art_of_Letting_Go_SINGLE_announcement_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Art_of_Letting_Go_SINGLE_announcement-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> It was commercially unsuccessful, peaking at number 19 on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_Hot_100_Singles" title="Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles">Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/You%27re_Mine_(Eternal)" title="You're Mine (Eternal)">You're Mine (Eternal)</a>" was released as the third single on February 12, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Commercially, the song has had limited success, charting inside the top 40 in Hungary, Korea, and Spain. In the United States, the song peaked at number 88 on the Hot 100, but became Carey's 17th number-one single on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Club_Songs" title="Hot Dance Club Songs">Hot Dance Club Songs</a> chart, placing her in fifth position as the artist with most number-one songs on that chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-danceclub_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-danceclub-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/You_Don%27t_Know_What_to_Do" title="You Don't Know What to Do">You Don't Know What to Do</a>" impacted <a href="/wiki/Urban_contemporary" title="Urban contemporary">urban contemporary</a> radio on June 30, 2014 and <a href="/wiki/Rhythmic_contemporary" title="Rhythmic contemporary">rhythmic contemporary</a> radio on July 1, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MainstreamUrban_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-MainstreamUrban-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top40R_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Top40R-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<tr>
<td><i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i></td>
<td style="vertical-align:middle"><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="3.5/4 stars"><img alt="3.5/4 stars" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" title="3.5/4 stars" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Star_half.svg/11px-Star_half.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Star_half.svg/17px-Star_half.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Star_half.svg/22px-Star_half.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Upon release, the album received generally positive reviews. The review aggregator website <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a> gives a weighted average rating to an album based upon the selected independent mainstream reviews it utilizes, and the album has a Metascore of a 67 out of 100 based on 15 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metacritic_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a>, Andy Kellman rated the album three-and-a-half stars out of five, saying how Mariah has abandoned the brevity of her earlier releases, but says the songstress is "still capable of delivering 40 minutes of strong, supremely voiced R&amp;B when she's up for it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Kenneth Partridge of <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> rated the album a 77 out of 100, writing how Mariah has found her musical niche that her fans have come to expect that is a "mix of pop-classicist balladry and hip-hop-tinged summer jamming".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_49-10"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> At <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i>, Melissa Maerz graded the album a B, saying how the release proves that her voice has been put through its paces, which she writes when Mariah is "trying to power through a note where it sounds like digital technology might be holding her up by the straps of that crocheted swimsuit."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-entertainmentweekly_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-entertainmentweekly-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Gardner however, Mariah's vocal is "relaxed and confident".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Also, Sargent notes that Mariah has "rarely sounded as comfortable."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitchfork_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Jim Farber of <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" title="Daily News (New York)">New York Daily News</a></i> rated the album four stars out of five, writing how the title is not indicative of the release as a whole because he says Mariah is not "elusive" in the least on an album where she "made her talent more clear."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nydailynews_40-3"><a href="#cite_note-nydailynews-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> At <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>, Elysa Gardner rated the album three-and-a-half stars out of four, remarking whether "Elusive or not, this chanteuse is a survivor, and that's a rare thing in today's fickle, polarized pop landscape."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Glenn Gamboa of <i><a href="/wiki/Newsday" title="Newsday">Newsday</a></i> graded the album an A-, commenting how Mariah has "nailed it" because she "goes for timeless [sounding music], with grand results."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsday_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-newsday-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> At <i><a href="/wiki/The_Plain_Dealer" title="The Plain Dealer">The Plain Dealer</a></i>, Troy L. Smith graded the album a B, indicating how the music meanders towards the latter stages of the album, yet noting that Mariah still picks the correct collaborators to work with on the release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cleveland_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cleveland-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Maher however, the collaborations serve no purpose just showing how Mariah is "desperate[ly] skirting around for identity" that "leaves this album feeling underwhelming."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musicomh_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-musicomh-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> At <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i>, August Brown rated the album two-and-a-half stars out of four, indicating how Mariah vocally reined herself in on the album where she showcases her continued relevance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> Kevin Ritchie of <i><a href="/wiki/Now_(newspaper)" title="Now (newspaper)">Now</a></i> rated the album four N's out of five, finding out that "Carey's back to adding her sparkly touch to summer-ready pop tunes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-now_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-now-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork</a>, Jordan Sargent rated the album a 7.7 out of ten, giving her credit for not sounding "desperate" because the tonality is "defiantly like Mariah, acknowledging her place in the pop ecosystem both implicitly and explicitly without chomping at the bit."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitchfork_112-2"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Nick Murray of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> rated the album three stars out five, observing how "stylistic cohesion is as elusive as the chanteuse herself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> At <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, Caroline Sullivan rated the album three stars out of five, indicating how the release contains "a good deal of clutter", however, Mariah is "also at her most soulful and melodic" on a release she calls "a welcome return."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theguardian_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Eric Henderson of <a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a> rated the album three stars out of five, observing how the release is chalked full of ''<i>Un</i>disciplined R&amp;B pastiches."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slantmagazine_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-slantmagazine-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> At <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i>, Sarah Rodman gave a mixed review of the album, commenting on how even the good moments are "sabotaged", and the release as a whole is highly predictable with "a clutch of interchangeable slow-to-midtempo tunes long on pulsating atmosphere — several with distractingly fidgety rhythmic tracks — but short on melody or verve."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thebostonglobe_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-thebostonglobe-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> Aimee Cliff of <i><a href="/wiki/Fact_(UK_magazine)" title="Fact (UK magazine)">Fact</a></i> rated the album two-and-a-half discs out of five, comparing the album unfavorably to Beyoncé's <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_(album)" title="Beyoncé (album)">self-titled</a> writing that "the record just doesn’t have the same candid, bold edge that characterised Beyonce's huge statement."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fact_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-fact-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/MusicOMH" title="MusicOMH">musicOMH</a>, Amelia Maher rated the album two-and-a-half stars out of five, stating how Mariah's vocal range is undoubtedly robust, but this time around on the release she "falls short."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musicomh_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-musicomh-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chart_performance">Chart performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Chart performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the United States, the album debuted at number three on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> albums chart with sales of 58,000 copies. It is her 17th top-ten album in the US, but became her lowest opening for a non holiday studio album since <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> started tracking sales in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bb200_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-bb200-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> The album rapidly descended down the charts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> and was present on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 for a total of eight weeks, the shortest chart run for any of Carey's studio albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> As of December 2014, the album has sold 117,000 copies in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bb_dec2014_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-bb_dec2014-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Billboard</i> speculated that its high ratio of first-week sales to total 2014 sales suggested that interest in the album came primarily from a dwindling group of <a href="/wiki/Stan_(fan)" title="Stan (fan)">die-hard fans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bb_dec2014_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-bb_dec2014-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, in the United Kingdom, the album peaked at number fourteen on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>, with sales of 6,547 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> In its second week, the album plummeted to number 54, before falling off the Top 100 in its third week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<dl>
<dt>Notes</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_a">^a</a></b></span></sup> signifies an additional <a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">producer</a></li>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_b"><b><a href="#ref_b">^b</a></b></span></sup> signifies co-<a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">producer</a></li>
<li>"Dedicated" contains a sample from "Da Mystery of Chessboxin'" as performed by <a href="/wiki/Wu-Tang_Clan" title="Wu-Tang Clan">Wu-Tang Clan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-7"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"Make It Look Good" contains interpolations of "Let Me Make Love to You", written by <a href="/wiki/Bunny_Sigler" title="Bunny Sigler">Walter "Bunny" Sigler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allan_Felder" title="Allan Felder">Allan Felder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-8"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"You Don't Know What to Do" contains interpolations of "I'm Caught Up in a One Night Love Affair", written by <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Adams_(musician)" title="Patrick Adams (musician)">Patrick Adams</a> and Terri Gonzalez.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-9"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"Meteorite" contains a sample from "Goin' Up in Smoke", performed by Eddie Kendricks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-10"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"Money" is stylized as "Money ($ * / ...)". It also features a sample from "Alabeke", performed by Dan Snatch, and "Rapper Dapper Snapper" performed by Edwin Birdsong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-11"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"One More Try" is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cover_song" title="Cover song">cover</a> of <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>'s 1988 single <a href="/wiki/One_More_Try_(George_Michael_song)" title="One More Try (George Michael song)">of the same name</a>.</li>
<li>"Heavenly (No Way Tired / Can't Give Up Now)" is dedicated as a tribute to the late Reverend <a href="/wiki/James_Cleveland" title="James Cleveland">James Cleveland</a>. It contains an excerpt from the Reverend's sermon "God's Promise" performed by James Cleveland. Also contains a sample of "Can't Give Up Now" performed by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Mary" title="Mary Mary">Mary Mary</a>, "I Don't Feel No Ways Tired" performed by James Cleveland and "Good Ole Music" performed by <a href="/wiki/Funkadelic" title="Funkadelic">Funkadelic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-12"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"It's a Wrap" contains a sample of "I Belong to You" by <a href="/wiki/Barry_White" title="Barry White">Barry White</a>, performed by the Love Unlimited Orchestra.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Booklet_51-13"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Booklet-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In Japan, only one version of the album was released on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compact_Disc" title="Compact Disc">Compact Disc</a> (CD); it features all of the songs from the digital deluxe edition except for the title track "Me. I Am Mariah... The Elusive Chanteuse", which is replaced with an exclusive bonus track, "<a href="/wiki/America_the_Beautiful" title="America the Beautiful">America the Beautiful</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jap_CD_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jap_CD-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> This version of the album was also released as an exclusive at <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a> stores in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Target_CD_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-Target_CD-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The title track is only included on digital editions of the album; it is not included on physical editions, as it is Mariah reading what is printed beneath the disc tray of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewel_case" title="Jewel case">jewel case</a>.</li>
</ul>
